\\tRemove(path string) error\\n98: }\\n99: type noopWatcher struct{}\\n100: \\n101: func (noopWatcher) Add(path string) error    { return nil }\\n102: func (noopWatcher) Remove(path string) error { return nil }\\n103: \\n104: // WatchUntil watches the specified path for changes and blocks until ctx is canceled.\\n105: // eventHandler() must be non-nil, and pollInterval must be greater than 0.\\n106: // eventHandler() is invoked whenever a change event is observed or pollInterval elapses.\\n107: // errorHandler() is invoked (if non-nil) whenever an error occurs initializing or watching the specified path.\\n108: //\\n109: // If path is a directory, only the directory and immediate children are watched.\\n110: //\\n111: // If path does not exist or cannot be watched, an error is passed to errorHandler() and eventHandler() is called at pollInterval.\\n112: //\\n113: // Multiple observed events may collapse to a single invocation of eventHandler().\\n114: //\\n115: // eventHandler() is invoked immediately after successful initialization of the filesystem watch,\\n116: // in case the path changed concurrent with calling WatchUntil().\\n117: func WatchUntil(ctx \\t\\tattemptPeriodicRewatch = true\\n156: \\t} else {\\n157: \\t\\t// Invoke handle() at least once after successfully registering the listener,\\n158: \\t\\t// in case the file changed concurrent configuration hot-reload for encryption configuration without restarting the API server using three key components:\\n\\n**1. File Watcher Setup (pkg/util/filesystem/watcher.go:WatchUntil)**\\nThe `WatchUntil()` function provides a callback-based filesystem watcher that combines fsnotify for event-driven updates with periodic polling as a fallback. It watches a specified file path and invokes an event handler whenever a change is observed or a poll interval elapses. This dual approach ensures file changes are detected reliably even if fsnotify encounters errors.\\n\\n**2. Config Diff Detection (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/options/encryptionconfig/controller/controller.go)**\\nThe `DynamicEncryptionConfigContent` controller implements a rate-limited queue pattern (via Kubernetes workqueue). It polls for changes using `EncryptionConfigFileChangePollDuration` (default 1 minute) and detects configuration changes by comparing SHA256 hashes:\\n- `processEncryptionConfig()` first checks if the file hash has changed before attempting to load\\n- If hash differs, it loads the new configuration and validates it\\n- After successful load, it compares hashes again (TOCTOU protection) to ensure the config is truly new\\n- Only if both checks show a difference does it proceed with the swap\\n\\nHash computation is done via `GetEncryptionConfigHash()` in config.go:556, which reads the file and computes `sha256:hexdigest`.\\n\\n**3. Atomic Config Swap (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/options/encryptionconfig/config.go)**\\nThe `DynamicTransformers` struct uses `atomic.Value` (line 923) to achieve lock-free reads. The `Set()` method (lines 974-998):\\n- Creates a new `transformTracker` struct containing the new transformers and health check\\n- Atomically swaps the old tracker for the new one using `atomic.Value.Swap()` (line 989)\\n- After swap, all new requests immediately use the new transformers (no locks held)\\n- Old transformers are closed asynchronously after a grace period (`kmsCloseGracePeriod`), allowing in-flight requests to complete\\n\\nThe reload workflow is orchestrated by the controller's `Run()` method which calls through `processEncryptionConfig()` → `validateNewTransformersHealth()` → `dynamicTransformers.Set()`, ensuring new transformers are healthy before swapping.\\n\\n**Authorization Config Reload (pkg/kubeapiserver/authorizer/reload.go)**\\nA parallel pattern is used for authorization configuration:\\n- `runReload()` uses `filesystem.WatchUntil()` with a configurable `reloadInterval`\\n- `checkFile()` compares file contents byte-by-byte and validates the parsed configuration\\n- Uses `atomic.Pointer[authorizerResolver]` to atomically swap the entire authorizer chain via `Store()` (line 248)\\n\\n### Prometheus: Configuration Hot-Reload with Auto-Detection\\n\\nPrometheus implements configuration hot-reload triggered by both manual signals (SIGHUP, /-/reload API) and automatic change detection:\\n\\n**1. File Watcher Setup (discovery/file/file.go)**\\nThe file discovery component uses `fsnotify.NewWatcher()` to watch configuration files. In cmd/prometheus/main.go, the reload handler monitors for file changes via `time.Tick()` at intervals specified by `--config.auto-reload-interval` (default 30s).\\n\\n**2. Config Diff Detection (config/reload.go:GenerateChecksum)**\\nThe `GenerateChecksum()` function computes a SHA256 hash covering:\\n- The main configuration file content\\n- All referenced rule files (matched via glob patterns from `rule_files` config)\\n- All referenced scrape config files (matched via glob patterns from `scrape_config_files` config)\\n- File paths and contents are hashed in a deterministic order\\n\\nThe reload loop in cmd/prometheus/main.go (lines 1313-1330) compares checksums at each interval and only proceeds with reload if `currentChecksum != checksum`.\\n\\n**3. Atomic Config Swap (cmd/prometheus/main.go:reloadConfig + scrape/manager.go:ApplyConfig)**\\nThe `reloadConfig()` function (lines 1600-1645) performs sequential reloads of all configuration consumers via the `reloaders` slice:\\n- Parses the new configuration using `config.LoadFile()`\\n- Iterates through reloaders in order: scrape manager, rule manager, discovery manager, etc.\\n- Each reloader's `ApplyConfig()` method handles atomic updates\\n\\nThe scrape manager's `ApplyConfig()` (scrape/manager.go:279) demonstrates the swap pattern:\\n- Takes exclusive lock on `mtxScrape`\\n- Validates all new scrape configurations\\n- For each pool, determines if it needs reload by comparing with `reflect.DeepEqual(sp.config, cfg)`\\n- Spawns goroutines to reload pools in parallel (limited by `runtime.GOMAXPROCS(0)`)\\n- Deletes pools removed from configuration\\n- Unlocks and waits for all reload goroutines to complete\\n- Old scrape pools are stopped cleanly while new ones start, and the reload handler invokes discovery manager to fetch new targets\\n\\nThe reload callback (line 1277) updates metrics and notifications based on success/failure. If reload fails, existing configuration remains in use and is not updated.\\n\\n### Key Differences\\n\\n**Kubernetes** emphasizes:\\n- Lock-free reads using `atomic.Value` for zero-impact request path during reload\\n- Grace period for closing old resources, allowing in-flight requests to complete\\n- Health checking of new transformers before swapping\\n\\n**Prometheus** emphasizes:\\n- Deterministic multi-file checksums including rule and scrape config files\\n- Ordered reload sequence across multiple configuration consumers\\n- Parallel reload of scrape pools with concurrency limiting\\n- Clean cascade through discovery manager to fetch new targets\\n\\nBoth use polling with configurable intervals as the primary change detection mechanism, with fsnotify as an optional event-driven enhancement.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":12,"cache_creation_input_tokens":5734,"cache_read_input_tokens":89146,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":5734},"output_tokens":3,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"28d34ae1-dc70-45e6-b2a4-b3636bd2c55a","uuid":"1f36048a-e9e5-4a4d-b4dd-0a8f033f7b7a"}
